Supplement to the Shanghai News

Opinions

An Account of Children's Education 209

— Buddha

Today is already the 14th of August. The notice from the Municipal Education Bureau about the start of the school term is not far off. Fathers and elder brothers must once again plan a sum for education expenses to send their children to school. Therefore, I will calculate the school fees and study time of children.

Let's not calculate elementary school. I will calculate middle school and university. For middle school, each semester's tuition, board, and lodging for one student costs at least eighty or ninety yuan, and as much as over one hundred yuan. In addition, there are expenses for books, pocket money, laundry, etc., requiring about one hundred and fifty-two yuan per semester. These students are not considered particularly extravagant. As for university students, naturally, it costs even more. Each semester requires no less than two hundred yuan. Therefore, for one student, three years of junior high and three years of senior high require one thousand eight hundred yuan to buy a middle school diploma. Adding four years of university requires another one thousand six hundred yuan to buy a university diploma. If the child is unwilling to study hard or is of dull aptitude, not counting any potential need for additional years, then one student requires three to four thousand yuan to graduate from middle school and university. With such aristocratic schools, how many people can afford to study?

Fathers and elder brothers spend such a large sum on education expenses, and then I calculate the students' study time. In one year, there is about one month for the New Year holiday, about one week or ten days for the spring break, and another two months or more for the summer vacation. Besides these, there are Sundays, various commemorative days, or sports meets, which also lead to holidays. Deducting these, one only truly studies for at most six months each year. Though nominally ten years are spent in middle school and university, in reality, one only truly studies for five years. This also doesn't account for truly unprofessional schools. If one unfortunately encounters patriotic movements or school disturbances, such temporary wastage of studies is not even included in the calculation.

Therefore, for a student to graduate from a domestic university, including six years of elementary school fees, requires four thousand yuan. Studying abroad is out of the question. Assuming you have three children, you need no less than twelve thousand yuan for education expenses. Assuming you have four children, you need no less than sixteen thousand yuan for education expenses. I ask, with such costs, can fathers and elder brothers still bear it?

Because the school fees are so large, and the profit margins so high, unprofessional schools have sprung up like bamboo shoots after the rain. Principals only know how to collect money and don't care about the students' studies. Every extra day of holiday means an extra meal for them. Teachers, fearing the instability of their jobs, merely go through the motions with the students and dare not be too strict. Therefore, although they are nominally university graduates, some cannot write proper Chinese, and some cannot write a simple English letter. I ask, how can such education not lead to bankruptcy?

People go bankrupt because of their children's education, and schools go bankrupt because of educational corruption. Especially, politicians often use the blind minds of young people as tools for contention and infighting. Therefore, school disturbances become more and more frequent. Fathers and elder brothers spend vast amounts of money, but students are unwilling to focus on their studies, instead waving flags and shouting slogans, engaging in meaningless activism. Alas, with such human hearts, what else can be said? With China like this, what cure is there? I can only be like reading Councilor Chen's speech, with the final sentence marking the end.

Arts and Literature

Visiting General Dai in Suzhou 210

— Right Year

In the winter of Xinwei, I visited General Dai in Suzhou. The General had just returned from suppressing bandits in southern Jiangxi. Such rivers and mountains, such a scene! Gusu (Suzhou) has been home to beautiful jade since ancient times. Returning now from suppressing bandits in Hongdu (Nanchang), he carries back a body stained with blood.

Inscribed on the wall of the General's quarters in Longhua:

The iron cavalry descended upon Shanghai, military headquarters opened in Longhua. Old friends appreciate lodging here. In the new spring, we watch the raising of banners. Silver seals follow commands, red brushes shame flowery words. Morning and evening we hear the drums of war. Living here deeply, we forget our homes.

Science

Various Printing Methods 211

— Fumin

(1) Postcard Printing Method: There are many postcard printing methods. The simplest is to use lamp-light paper to make postcards. I often imitate this method and have found it quite effective. This type of postcard paper cannot be exposed to light, so it should be wrapped in black paper for normal use. When needed, choose a spot near a kerosene lamp, about four or five feet away, where there is no direct strong light. Unfold the paper package, place the negative on top, and place a large wooden board underneath. Use four bamboo strips to clamp the two sides (or a photo frame can also be used). Place it at an angle, five or six inches from the lamp, allowing it to receive light for about one minute. Then, release the bamboo strips and take out the paper. At this time, there is no image on the paper. It must be immersed in developing solution for several hours before an image appears. After developing, wash it with clean water and immerse it in a sodium sulfite solution (one part sodium sulfite to ten parts water) for about ten minutes. Take it out, wait for it to dry, and then re-wet it. Finally, paste it onto a clean glass slide and dry it slowly.

After drying, it can be peeled off, and a photographic postcard is complete.

(2) Teapot Printing Method: Use a bristle brush to remove stains from the surface of a teapot. Slowly coat it with animal glue (glue made by boiling animal skin and bones) in an oval shape. After it dries, add a layer of silver nitrate solution (one part nitric acid to nine parts water). Place the negative on the coated surface, tie it tightly with string, and place it horizontally in the sunlight for one minute until the image appears. Then, remove the negative and use a bristle brush dipped in plenty of clean water to wash the surface of the teapot. When a white mist appears, wash it away with water. Moisten it with borax water and gold chloride solution, then the image will appear reddish-brown. When it turns purple, wash it again with water, and the image will be fixed on the surface. Allow it to dry slowly. This method can be used for printing images on porcelain items such as bowls and basins. However, if the surface of the porcelain is round or uneven, it will be difficult to apply the negative closely to the surface, making it difficult to develop a clear image.

(3) Handkerchief Printing Method: Soak the handkerchief (any kind of handkerchief except towels) in soapy water to wash away grease. After it dries, use a brush to apply silver nitrate solution to its surface. There is no fixed method; you can make a circle, oval, square, polygon, or apply it in a corner or in the center, all are acceptable. However, the amount applied should be even, not biased. After application, place it in a dark place to dry in the shade. When printing, take a piece of black, firm paper, cut out square or round holes in the middle, and place it between the negative and the handkerchief. Place them together in a printing frame and expose them to the sun. When the image is deep enough, take out the handkerchief and process it according to the teapot printing method. However, all washing and other processes should be done by immersing it in the solution.

Social Improvement Discussion Group

Abolishing Smoking, Drinking, and Gambling as Social Customs 212

— Yiping

Relationships arise between people, and customs are passed down. Whenever there are weddings, funerals, or other celebratory events, it is customary to exchange gifts and socialize. Therefore, the host family must prepare cigarettes and alcohol to entertain guests, and mahjong, the most popular form of gambling, is an indispensable item in social gatherings. There are already proposals from comrades in this association to improve social customs, and the elimination of bad habits such as smoking, drinking, and gambling is all the more urgent.

The harms are briefly described below.

(1) Smoking: In ordinary interactions between friends, offering a cigarette is very common. It can be said that everyone in the country can puff on one. However, cigarettes contain nicotine, which is not only irritating but also easily damages the lungs. Although you don't feel anything while smoking, it is very harmful in the long run. In social gatherings, people even prepare opium. In the host's mind, it's just for fun, but the harm of smoking opium is of course known to everyone and is also illegal (before the formal opium monopoly, I could still say this).

(2) Drinking: Like cigarettes, a few friends can meet and get drunk at Gao Changxing's or Ma Shanghou's place. When a family has an event, they will force guests to drink another cup. The harm is as described above. Currently, many movies even teach spoiled sons how to violate the chastity of women, such as Li Baozhen in "Married Woman" and Luo Xia in "Fallen Hate." Movies have performances by big stars, so naturally such things happen in society as well.

(3) Gambling: I am particularly referring to mahjong. Mahjong is a national treasure of China, and it is now fashionable in Europe and America, where people think that being able to play mahjong is fashionable. Families with children instill in them a desire for luck, deeply imprinting the idea of gambling in their young minds. Women are even more enthusiastic about it, destroying family happiness and leading to bankruptcy, which is also expected.

Therefore, members of this association specifically propose this for discussion and guidance.

The Question of Gender Equality 213

— Zhen

Has the issue of gender equality already been resolved? Otherwise, why haven't we seen any discussions about it for so long? The reason why I bring up this issue for everyone to discuss is that I believe the issue of gender equality is still an open question that has not been resolved. If you don't believe me, please look at the following facts:

First, let's talk about old-style women. The so-called old-style women refer to those women who have not studied Western knowledge, learned modern ways, and still believe in the three obediences and four virtues. They still hold the old concepts of obeying their fathers at home, obeying their husbands after marriage, and obeying their sons after their husbands die, living a muddled life. They are truly like the ancients said, "not knowing there was Han, let alone Wei and Jin." Everything depends on men, so naturally, there is no gender equality to speak of.

It is a fact that old-style women are still slaves of men, and there is no need to deny it. Let's look at how new-style women are. The so-called new-style women, of course, refer to those women who have studied Western knowledge, are good at modern ways, and extremely believe in the liberation of women (?). They have studied Western knowledge and can write some mushy letters like "Dearest Brother," "My Most Beloved," "My...," and can say some seductive words like "My dear, I love you," "Kiss me..." They live a life of drunken stupor every day. Clothing, food, housing, and everything they use are provided by men. It is still a life of dependence. The only difference from old-style women is that old-style women have to manage household affairs and don't know how to have fun, while new-style women can ignore household affairs and enjoy themselves to the fullest. The former can be said to be the slaves of men, and the latter can be said to be the toys of men. In short, they are not people, not people who are equal to men.

There is another type of new-style women, which can be said to be a separate faction of new-style women. Of course, this faction of women has also studied Western knowledge, is not very modern, and knows that to be equal to men, they must seek economic independence. Therefore, they also serve in society and have considerable professions. This faction of women's thinking is extremely new. If there is no production, it is inevitable to become a slave of men, and modernization becomes a toy of men. But the money they earn is their own, and the burden of the family is still pushed onto the men. Occasionally, when the husband's income is not enough, or when he is unemployed, and needs the woman's help a little, then these women consider it a favor to the men, not an obligation that should be fulfilled. It is difficult to be seen without modern clothes, and modernization becomes a toy of men. So they come up with a compromise. Only new-style women who have studied Western knowledge can come up with this: they also make one or two modern clothes, specifically for going out to let the people on the street to see, while at home they wear ragged clothes and unkempt hair, leaving it for the husband to see.

Gentlemen, think about the issue of gender equality. How should it be resolved in the end? Or should we just leave it like this?

Truly!

Love and Money 214

— Yinong

I remember a summer day last year, in the sweltering heat. I took some time out of my busy schedule to visit an old classmate, Mr. A, who lived in a garret in a small alley in the French Concession. Mr. A, my old classmate, was my most respected and feared beneficial friend. He carried the full range of abilities and was full of determination. He had mixed in the dirty political arena for several years. His performance was very good! He gained both fame and fortune. He and his "she"—two little girls—lived a sweet life. Husband sang, wife followed, a happy and harmonious family. It was indeed worthy of admiration.

The tide of economic downturn spread to the unfortunate Mr. A. Salary arrears, pay cuts, layoffs, and ultimately unemployment. Their family's life gradually contracted. When it was tightened as much as possible and shrunk as much as possible, problems ultimately arose.

As a result of tightening, they no longer lived in a single-family small Western-style house and went to live in that steamer-like garret. They could not eat fully nourishing food, could not wear suitable clothes, and had no share in entertainment that could nourish their body and mind. It was indeed difficult for them to survive in such a bad environment. When I walked into Mr. A's bedroom, I saw that Mr. A was still lying on a small wooden bed in this hot weather. His pale face and short breath indicated that he was ill. His wife, Ms. T, was well-educated and had a thorough outlook on life. She had gone through a love process and held a grand wedding. In the three years of love crystallization, they already had two little girls. Now, she was knitting her eyebrows and sitting on a half-old cloth couch, coaxing the two little children. When Mr. A saw me walking into his bedroom, he hurriedly called me to sit by his bed, and in a trembling voice, said to me:

"Yi! Marriage is the tomb of love! This sentence is absolutely correct. Before we got married, how sweet it was. The foundation of our union was built on spirit, not on material things. Who knew that today, the spirit is still this spirit, but the material things are very different. That is, our love is about to change. I, who am added with disease and poverty, must not strive from the material perspective, I am afraid that I will not be able to maintain this kind of love. The ancients said that love between husband and wife is called the joy of fish and water. I say that love is fish, and money is water. Fish cannot survive without water. Without the help of money, I am afraid that love will be difficult to last?"

After listening to his words, I told him not to be too sentimental and think too much. It was most important to be at ease and rest quietly. I also advised Ms. T not to have a rift because of these indignant words of the patient. It is necessary to understand each other. Although Ms. T did not say anything, according to what I knew, she did say a lot of complaints because of this environment, such as "Without me, you wouldn't have suffered this kind of family burden, I am hurting you." Mr. A, of course, could not be completely without feeling when he heard these words.

The night before, I was walking alone along the smooth Yuyuan Road. A refined red building reflected green lights. As the iron gate opened, a couple walked out very smartly. Taking a closer look, this was my old classmate Mr. A, accompanied by his she Ms. T.

Page 20

When they saw me, they called me to their home and chatted in a small living room. I then learned that Mr. A had obtained a suitable position after his illness last year and had restored his old life. However, Mr. A always maintained his prejudice,

Love is fish, money is water, water can feed fish, fish cannot leave water!

Initial Diagnosis — Yiping 215

Venereal diseases are increasing rapidly in Shanghai. A certain doctor, skilled in speculative management, actually became a wealthy man. So, near the French Concession, he rented two houses, one as a hospital and one as a pharmacy, both inscribed with his own name. He also widely installed X-ray lamps, sun lamps, etc., and many people promoted him. Business was booming. Because of his publicity, I also visited for the first time. In a corner of the waiting room, there was a registration desk. (Registration fee two yuan.) That black-robed figure, like an informant, said to me. I paid two dollars. "Initial visit or follow-up visit?" He probably influenced by the master (please see the following). He asked me in a commanding tone: "Initial visit," I said. He gave me an initial visit token and a copper plate with number forty-eight. At this time, there were more than a dozen patients waiting in the waiting room, treated according to their number. Now only number thirty-two was reached. Helpless, I took a walk nearby, waiting and waiting. Two hours later, it was number forty-eight's turn. I stepped into the examination room. It was a wing room equipped with advanced medical equipment. The nurse took the copper plate and asked me to sit on a white painted stool next to Dr. So-and-so. He began to ask me: "What's wrong?" "Lung disease." "Seen a doctor in the countryside?" "Taken any medicine?" Asking here, he filled in something on a printed paper.

"Had injections?" "What kind of liquid?" He continued to write, without even looking at me. "XXXX (a kind of lung disease liquid)." "Hmm." (Seemed suspicious.) "Have chills and fever?" "No." "Cough?" "In the morning." "Have phlegm?" "Yes." "Have blood?" "No." Then he ordered something, and the nurse put a thermometer in my mouth. He continued to write. Three minutes later, the nurse reported: "37.3 degrees." "Have chills and fever!" He seemed to be talking to himself, while at the same time accusing me of lying.

Then he just examined my chest, listened roughly, tapped with his fingers once. "Lung breathing power too weak, first reduce chills and fever first."

He filled in a printed paper again. "Is it lung disease?" I asked in doubt. "Yes."

"What stage?"

"Hmm... hmm... approximately (note, doctors can use 'approximately' tone) the second stage." "Where is it bad?"

"The apex of the lung." "Is the lower part intact?" "Approximately (note again) intact." "What happens after taking the medicine for reducing chills and fever?" "First take an X-ray."

I wanted to ask again, but the nurse shouted for number forty-nine to come in for interrogation. I was forced into the pharmacy next door and bought the medicine. They didn't give me the prescription.

"Where's the prescription?" "It's kept here, ready for follow-up visits for comparison."

From the above, one can imagine how terrible it is to see a doctor in Shanghai. The diagnosis is all obtained in an interrogation,

and still cannot determine what disease this is. There is no prescription, and the patient cannot negotiate after taking the wrong medicine. So my initial visit is finally an initial visit, approximately (no need to pay attention), he is still waiting for me to take an X-ray.

(The above were issued on August 12th) ▲Proclamation Regarding the proclamation matter, the Jiangsu High Court's Order No. 791 and the Ministry of Justice's Administrative Order No. 1708 state that, according to law, simple cases may be prosecuted orally. In the past, state and county officials would accept cases based on verbal accusations. Recently, however, it has been observed that courts often require written statements even for simple cases, causing inconvenience to the parties involved and failing to adhere to the provisions of the law. In order to seek truth from facts, the Ministry of Justice, for the sake of promoting industry, orders that all courts must transcribe and print multiple copies of the various items listed in Article 393 of the Civil Procedure Law, which allow for oral prosecution. These copies must be posted on the doors of the courts and published in local newspapers so that the public is aware of them. Hereafter, minor lawsuits, whether for prosecution, declaration, or statement, may be made orally and need not be limited to written form, thereby complying with the wishes of the people and upholding the law. It is ordered that the court comply with this order and instruct its subordinates to comply and handle accordingly. Therefore, this proclamation is issued, along with a full transcript of Article 393 of the Civil Procedure Law, so that all litigants are fully informed. This proclamation is hereby issued. Attached is the text of Article 393. Article 393 Regarding lawsuits involving property rights, the simple procedures specified in this chapter shall apply to cases where the amount or value of the subject matter is less than 800 yuan. The following types of lawsuits, even if the amount or value of the subject matter exceeds 800 yuan, shall also be subject to the simple procedures: 1. Lawsuits involving landlords or tenants regarding the receipt of houses or the relocation of use, repairs, or the withholding of tenants' furniture and goods. 2. Lawsuits between employers and employees arising from employment contracts with employment periods of one year or less. 3. Lawsuits between travelers and innkeepers, restaurant owners, or transporters regarding food, lodging, transportation fees, or the safekeeping of luggage and property. 4. Lawsuits arising from requests for protection of possession. 5. Lawsuits arising from the determination of boundary lines or the establishment of landmarks on real estate. 6. Other lawsuits where the parties agree to apply the simple procedures. August 13, 21st year of the Republic of China. Court President Shen Jianqing. (The above was issued on June 13th)
